  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_66be71de-ac5f-4903-9f46-1f6ae7293dcc'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_615').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/51948934-every-seventh-wave">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those ready to surf the seventh wave</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18383778-dolors?shelf=read-before-2011">read-before-2011</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2947388917" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16579376478919212578">This is the second installment of <i>âGut gegen Nordwindâ</i>, in my opinion objectionably translated <i>"Love Virtuallyâ</i> in English. Itâs a real pity because I believe a great deal of the bookâs personality is transmitted in the title, which is beautiful in its original language.<br/>I read both novels several years ago almost in one sitting and forgot about them till this summer, when I stumbled upon them by chance. One book canât be read without the other, and they need to be read in order. <br/>As I started to </span>
  <span id="freeText16579376478919212578" style="display:none">This is the second installment of <i>âGut gegen Nordwindâ</i>, in my opinion objectionably translated <i>"Love Virtuallyâ</i> in English. Itâs a real pity because I believe a great deal of the bookâs personality is transmitted in the title, which is beautiful in its original language.<br />I read both novels several years ago almost in one sitting and forgot about them till this summer, when I stumbled upon them by chance. One book canât be read without the other, and they need to be read in order. <br />As I started to browse the pages and read a sentence here and there, I realized I kept on reading till the end of each page, and onto the next, and the next, and a whole chapter was finished, and I didnât want to stop.<br />So considered forewarned. These are extremely addictive novels, and once you start, you might have the urge to finish both books at once, eager to lose a few hours of sleep to see how it all ends.<br /><br />Emmi and Leo are two middle-aged strangers who meet accidentally online and fall in love in spite of their personal circumstances. One is happily married with children, the other is getting over a recent break-up. Protected by the anonymity of the screen, humorous flirtation gradually gives way to plain honesty and as the pace of the emails becomes more and more frenetic, the ârealâ lives of Emmi and Leo have to confront the implications of their virtual correspondence.<br /><br />I know. The plot sounds as clichÃ©d as it might get, used to death, possibly superficial and with small potential for good storytelling. Well, it isnât.<br />Glattauer takes great pain to create a modern epistolary novel that vibrates with the fast, intelligent and tasteful dialogue between two people who have no idea where they are getting into. The exchanges are as sparkling as profound, and the written letters end up becoming voices that faithfully reveal the temperament of each character.<br />Email correspondence might seem a bit outdated today when we have access to internet from our smartphones at all hours, but the charactersâ effervescent personalities, their elegant humor, the situation they find themselves in and their reactions to the evolving events are so well portrayed, so carefully developed that itâs easy to think of Emmi and Leo as real people. The reader can't help caring for them, wanting them to take the leap, to trust their instincts and forget about what they believe is morally right.<br /><br />Glattauer has a refined sense of what it is to fall in love. The doubts, the fear, the anxiety that comes with it. Itâs like a sickness, a feverish state that clouds vision and often leads to foolish decisions. The success of these novels lays in the way Emmi and Leo live through this âafflictionâ; their circumstances and expectations are vastly dissimilar and so they need to be brave enough to admit their involvement with each other without compromising their realities. Or they need to be prepared to toss their realities to create a new one together. Easy said, not so easy done, right?<br /><br />The outcome of the affair couldnât be more realistic. Heart-warming and unpredictable too, like the seventh wave. There is this saying that the balanced sway of the first six waves lapping gently on the shore is sometimes broken by the unexpected force of the seventh. Its rebellious nature sweeps you away, leaving only the feeling of being dragged by it, hurt and a bit bruised maybe, but also energized to stand the monotony of the following six waves until the seventh comes back again... to change everything, maybe for good.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8430234530145880006">Every Seventh Wave is a sequel to the book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12640615.Love_Virtually' title='Love Virtually by Daniel Glattauer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Love Virtually</a>. <br/><br/><br/>I loved Love Virtually! It was fun, quirky, bittersweet...all those wonderful ingredients that make a rom-com <b>pop</b>!!! It had a great ending. Sort of open-ended that left a lot up to the reader's imagination and <i>really</i> left me wanting more. However beware what you wish for as sometimes more is not what a book needs! <br/><br/><br/>This sequel was so disappointing! It felt so uninspired. Plot lines and devices used in the first book that once felt so fres</span>
  <span id="freeText8430234530145880006" style="display:none">Every Seventh Wave is a sequel to the book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12640615.Love_Virtually" title="Love Virtually by Daniel Glattauer" rel="nofollow noopener">Love Virtually</a>. <br /><br /><br />I loved Love Virtually! It was fun, quirky, bittersweet...all those wonderful ingredients that make a rom-com <b>pop</b>!!! It had a great ending. Sort of open-ended that left a lot up to the reader's imagination and <i>really</i> left me wanting more. However beware what you wish for as sometimes more is not what a book needs! <br /><br /><br />This sequel was so disappointing! It felt so uninspired. Plot lines and devices used in the first book that once felt so fresh now felt tired. The story lacked the originality of the first because it attempted to repeat or at least model itself in its image: the characters never grew or didn't seem to learn anything from the exchanges they shared in book one. Where character flaws were cute and quirky in Love Virtually, here they quickly grew tiresome and irritating. The whole plot line felt as if the main characters were stuck running inside one of those constantly moving hamster wheels. Where Love Virtually was a quick and snappy read, this one just dragged and took me daaaaaaaaaaays to (force myself to) finish. <br /><br />Sadly, for me, this book was a letdown and I wish I had let the story of Emmi and Leo end with Love Virtually. <br /><br /><br /><b>one star</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3098338685283261180">aaaaaaawwww!!!<br/>I had no idea if the author would be able to create a book as good as the first one... and right now I'm not sure if we can actually compare them since they're both so very different.<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8431866.Contra_el_viento_del_norte__Contra_el_viento_del_norte___1_' title='Contra el viento del norte (Contra el viento del norte, #1) by Daniel Glattauer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Contra el viento del norte</a> truly is an amazing book, it's cleverly written and the ending is.. just... genius!, it makes the book twice as good.<br/>And now this second book was just as funny, witty, frustrating, sad and so much more.. in the end, I think you actually can't compare them, for me it's more li</span>
  <span id="freeText3098338685283261180" style="display:none">aaaaaaawwww!!!<br />I had no idea if the author would be able to create a book as good as the first one... and right now I'm not sure if we can actually compare them since they're both so very different.<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8431866.Contra_el_viento_del_norte__Contra_el_viento_del_norte___1_" title="Contra el viento del norte (Contra el viento del norte, #1) by Daniel Glattauer" rel="nofollow noopener">Contra el viento del norte</a> truly is an amazing book, it's cleverly written and the ending is.. just... genius!, it makes the book twice as good.<br />And now this second book was just as funny, witty, frustrating, sad and so much more.. in the end, I think you actually can't compare them, for me it's more like they both make ONE story, the first book was incomplete, the characters didn't have any kind of closure, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9548321.Cada_siete_olas__Contra_el_viento_del_norte___2_" title="Cada siete olas (Contra el viento del norte, #2) by Daniel Glattauer" rel="nofollow noopener">Cada siete olas</a> gives that to us.<br /><br />Truly, a roller coaster of emotions.</span>

<div id="review_321364095" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/321364095" />
    <a title="Lily Smalls" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4015250-lily-smalls"><img alt="Lily Smalls" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1322167007p2/4015250.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/321364095?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lily Smalls" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lily Smalls" href="/user/show/4015250-lily-smalls">Lily Smalls</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4015250-lily-smalls?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321364095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5145987562625869148"><p>I don't like sequels. Usually. What about <i>Alle sieben Wellen</i>, the sequel to <i>Gut gegen Nordwind</i>? Is it the exception to the rule? I'm finding it hard to make my mind up. I'd love to say yes, yes, yes but there is a slight tendency towards a clear no.</p>As the end of <i>Gut gegen Nordwind</i> was tough but in my opinion absolutely perfect, I started reading the follow-up with mixed feelings. Before I continue I better let you know what happens in both novels. By chance Leo and Emmi started an e-mail corresp</span>
  <span id="freeText5145987562625869148" style="display:none"><p>I don't like sequels. Usually. What about <i>Alle sieben Wellen</i>, the sequel to <i>Gut gegen Nordwind</i>? Is it the exception to the rule? I'm finding it hard to make my mind up. I'd love to say yes, yes, yes but there is a slight tendency towards a clear no.</p>As the end of <i>Gut gegen Nordwind</i> was tough but in my opinion absolutely perfect, I started reading the follow-up with mixed feelings. Before I continue I better let you know what happens in both novels. By chance Leo and Emmi started an e-mail correspondence and a virtual relationship. Every now and then they considered to meet up but actually feared a disappointment because of their too high expectations. Beyond that, there seems to be no chance for a relationship anyway. Emmi is happily married and can't imagine to leave her family. She feels too much responsability. On top of it her husband discovers her secret and interferes allowing Leo to meet his wife once, only to leave her alone afterwards. Leo gives in and decides on a clear cut with Emmi and a new start in Boston. This is where the second novel sets in. Over nine months Emmi corresponds with Leo's system administrator until Leo finally returns from Boston and starts sending distant replies. Leo is now in a relationship with Pamela and tries to elude Emmi. It takes a lot of mails and some encounters for Leo to discover that he is living a lie and yes this time the reader will partake in a happy end.<p>This was a basic summary which might gave you the false idea that both novels are trivial. On the contrary, there is not much of a background story. Both novels live on the two main character's voices, on there beautifully written love mails which do without any kitsch. They are genuine, honest, witty, inspiring, ironic, reliable and most of all exciting to follow. That applies at least to the first novel. As you can guess now, unfortunately, I have to say what worked the first time didn't work a second time. What fascinated in <i>Gut gegen Nordwind</i> palled on <i>Alle sieben Wellen</i>. Emmi's unique writing style, her numerations and analysis of Leo's psyche were still enjoyable to read but not as touching and, of course, not as unique any more. I'd rather avoid talking about Leo as I'm sorry to say that his character even wore out in the second novel. His voice was sometimes irritating and lost reliability. Altogether the plot seemed construed and interlaced with some obstacles to revive and elongate the correspondence between Emmi and Leo. I admit I once couldn't get enough of Emmi and Leo but as sad as I was when I finished <i>Gut gegen Nordwind</i> I was happy to be left with my own imagination of their story. So, it appeared to me as if the author with <i>Alle sieben Wellen</i> wanted to satisfy all those readers who couldn't live with an unhappy ending. Fair enough, I can see your objection, asking why I read <i>Alle sieben Wellen</i> in the first place. It was pure curiosity and the hope to be astonished once more.</p>To make it short. I wasn't drawn in. I wasn't even interested in finding out what future has in store for Emmi and Leo. It was too predictable. Whereas I devoured <i>Gut gegen Nordwind</i> I felt not much tension while reading its sequel. If it wasn't for Emmi I would have most probably left this book unfinished. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5145987562625869148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14545436372490909731">Love it. Even more than the previous one. Because... because it's that much more open, more appealing, more... more everything. And, although it's a sequel, this seems like a completely different story. New. Yes, there's Emmi. And Leo. Yes, they are (kind of) moving on. Yes, here's another roller coaster trip full of emotions, dreams, everything and anything you've been hoping for... and even more than that.<br/>And, yes, I disliked the ending of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1820716.Gut_gegen_Nordwind' title='Gut gegen Nordwind by Daniel Glattauer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gut gegen Nordwind</a>, but it was for the best. And maybe</span>
  <span id="freeText14545436372490909731" style="display:none">Love it. Even more than the previous one. Because... because it's that much more open, more appealing, more... more everything. And, although it's a sequel, this seems like a completely different story. New. Yes, there's Emmi. And Leo. Yes, they are (kind of) moving on. Yes, here's another roller coaster trip full of emotions, dreams, everything and anything you've been hoping for... and even more than that.<br />And, yes, I disliked the ending of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1820716.Gut_gegen_Nordwind" title="Gut gegen Nordwind by Daniel Glattauer" rel="nofollow noopener">Gut gegen Nordwind</a>, but it was for the best. And maybe, just maybe, this feels even better because of it. Now that I think about it... this was written by a man? Like, a real <i>male</i> man? Well, thank you Mr. Glattauer (twice) for making me believe there are still those Leo-kind-of guys out there. I needed that. And, wouldn't mind meeting one of them. Or, even better, e-mailing with one of them.<br />I enjoyed reading this book. Really, truly, immensely enjoyed. Wouldn't change a single thing, not even one letter, about it. Everything was (is) just as it should be. Perfect.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1903819583374356583">Cute, cute, cute! <br/>A year ago I read a book that was very sad and amazing. I could relate to that book a lot. Why? Because I had virtual friend and we really got close and understood each other on a deeper level. However, it wasn't really romantic, it was just different, without strings and objectively easy because that friend could give you another perspective of things from your life because he doesn't know you in person, hence he isn't subjective. <br/>The book was called 'Against northern wind' or</span>
  <span id="freeText1903819583374356583" style="display:none">Cute, cute, cute! <br />A year ago I read a book that was very sad and amazing. I could relate to that book a lot. Why? Because I had virtual friend and we really got close and understood each other on a deeper level. However, it wasn't really romantic, it was just different, without strings and objectively easy because that friend could give you another perspective of things from your life because he doesn't know you in person, hence he isn't subjective. <br />The book was called 'Against northern wind' or originally Gut gegen Norwind, and it was about two people that met each other on Internet accidentally when Emmi tried to cancel newspapers online. That's when she got an answer from Leo saying that she has wrong email adress. Bingo! The story begins. In a form of emails. It was really great and funny, light and sweet. Leo was so good with words, such a depth and wisdom, metaphors.. sometimes I didn't even know what he meant to say and got you thinking. <br /><br />Emmi was sweet but not happy in her life or marriage... and then comes Leo.<br /><br />And after a year or maybe two I find out there is a sequel. What could Daniel possibly say after that specific ending? I was curious so I read the second book. <br />What to say? It was good and short but I would stay with the first ending... Leo, how I like that man. He's amazing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1903819583374356583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

In some ways, Every Seventh Wave mana</span>
  <span id="freeText672913895633352188" style="display:none">Writing the sequel of a real good book is not an easy job at all but Daniel did it with aplomb. It has all the wit, homour and the essence of the first part which really makes it work. <br /><br />Every Seventh Wave begins exactly where Love Virtually ended..well, three weeks later! And finally the much awaited meeting does happen this time :) And that is how this book shapes up and moves. <br /><br />If you enjoyed Love Virtually, it almost follows that you will enjoy this sequel. In some ways, Every Seventh Wave managed to bring more depth and layers to a story that wasnât wholly uncomplicated from the outset. There is, I think, a darker undertone to this one that I definitely appreciated. Almost inevitably, there were also episodes that made the story more convenient than it was in the first book. <br /><br />So go for it; pick the first one if you haven't read that and then finish the entire virtual love story :)</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3210494581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11187570039588735544">The story of Emmi and Mike continues. A whirlwind of emotions, complications and unpredictably. The anxiety of being in love was still present in the letters. I kept reading, email after email. If I needed a practical ending, I would have asked the author to stop with the first book. But of course not. I needed a sequel and this delivered. It ended exactly the way I wanted it to. If you read the first book, you'd want to finish this one.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_996128951" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/996128951" />
    <a title="Ananya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2787475-ananya"><img alt="Ananya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374162782p2/2787475.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/996128951?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ananya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ananya" href="/user/show/2787475-ananya">Ananya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781906694982" href="/book/show/10339824-every-seventh-wave">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer996128951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6126897749697832858"><p>Finally! A year worth of wait can make you ravenous! This book did exactly that to me. Add to that, too much anticipation can leave you disappointed. A happy ending is what I wanted but not this way! Leo and Emmi share the same chemistry but their intense romance is unstable, fickle, inconsistent and lackadaisical (unfortunately, that's what I felt) for the reason that they're so confused in this book unlike in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9745480.Love_Virtually' title='Love Virtually by Daniel Glattauer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Love Virtually</a> ! But I enjoyed reading their characters through their mails and as it</p></span>
  <span id="freeText6126897749697832858" style="display:none"><p>Finally! A year worth of wait can make you ravenous! This book did exactly that to me. Add to that, too much anticipation can leave you disappointed. A happy ending is what I wanted but not this way! Leo and Emmi share the same chemistry but their intense romance is unstable, fickle, inconsistent and lackadaisical (unfortunately, that's what I felt) for the reason that they're so confused in this book unlike in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9745480.Love_Virtually" title="Love Virtually by Daniel Glattauer" rel="nofollow noopener">Love Virtually</a> ! But I enjoyed reading their characters through their mails and as it has been fittingly commented by <i>Independent on Sunday</i> - it's for the google generation. It's only "phase-2" of Emmi-Leo relationship so the theme and tone isn't different. I expected a lot from this book which I shouldn't have (but why not?!) so I'm a wee bit discontented.</p><p>
  <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Here's why. <b>Reason 1:</b> Emmi and Leo are not happily married. She's divorced from Bernhard but she's there for the family. They share the same flat but each is going about his own business. This defeats the entire purpose of being in a "family". That's why it's flawed. <i>The perfect scenario</i> - so much so that at one point I felt disconnected.<br /><b>Reason 2:</b> Emmi slept with Leo just because she had to, to drive home the point that she could cheat on Bernhard, which was unlike her personality. An impulsive one night stand would have been much more appealing.<br /><b>Reason 3:</b> Leo had lost his charm! Oh why!!! His silken voice, chivalry and discretion were 'in the doldrums' throughout that wasn't sexy at all. Thanks to his weakness for Emmi. Maybe it was justified in the context but I, as a reader could no longer seek "The Leo" I sought in Love Virtually. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</p><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <p>I still give this book 4 stars because I've been satiated. The story and the torturous hide-and-seek game between them has come to an end. They're not married and definitely don't live 'happily ever after' but the fact that they're together will do for now.</p>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="6126897749697832858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3827632590017265593">This is a very easy read, because it's in the form of exchanged e-mails. The only problem for me was that you have to assume what happens only based on the e-mails, and I found this a bit annoying at times. [SPOILER] However, it was obvious that the book would have a happy ending.   <span id="freeText3827632590017265593" style="display:none">This is a very easy read, because it's in the form of exchanged e-mails. The only problem for me was that you have to assume what happens only based on the e-mails, and I found this a bit annoying at times. [SPOILER] However, it was obvious that the book would have a happy ending. What I liked in particular was that both characters were believable and they both fought for what they wanted (or what they thought they wanted) in their own different ways. I liked that love was presented as a mixture of reason and choice. It wasn't some fairytale, it was realistic. I definitely recommend this book if you want to have a quiet night in - you can easily read it in one evening.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jfz4rdDUJsHkXr4KidRODKZAZGVRwh7SD+hC1k21qXYJ7aRSRs829Z9O0F29Bzgn9otOugddztxfntYhTeYCKA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
